<p><b>Friedrich Wilhelm Heinrich Alexander von Humboldt</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:De-Friedrich_Wilhelm_Heinrich_Alexander_Freiherr_von_Humboldt.oga" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/De-Friedrich_Wilhelm_Heinrich_Alexander_Freiherr_von_Humboldt.oga" class="internal" title="De-Friedrich Wilhelm Heinrich Alexander Freiherr von Humboldt.oga">listen</a></span>&#160;<small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:De-Friedrich_Wilhelm_Heinrich_Alexander_Freiherr_von_Humboldt.oga" title="File:De-Friedrich Wilhelm Heinrich Alexander Freiherr von Humboldt.oga"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span>; 14 September 1769&#160;– 6 May 1859) was a <a href="/wiki/Prussian" class="mw-redirect" title="Prussian">Prussian</a> <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geographer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">naturalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_explorers" title="List of explorers">explorer</a>, and influential proponent of <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> philosophy and <a href="/wiki/Romanticism_in_science" title="Romanticism in science">science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> He was the younger brother of the Prussian minister, philosopher, and <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguist</a> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm von Humboldt</a> (1767–1835).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Humboldt's quantitative work on <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botanical</a> <a href="/wiki/Geography" title="Geography">geography</a> laid the foundation for the field of <a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">biogeography</a>. Humboldt's advocacy of long-term systematic geophysical measurement laid the foundation for modern geomagnetic and meteorological monitoring.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 1799 and 1804, Humboldt travelled extensively in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, exploring and describing it for the first time from a modern scientific point of view. His description of the journey was written up and published in an enormous set of volumes over 21 years. Humboldt was one of the first people to propose that the lands bordering the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> were once joined (South America and Africa in particular). Humboldt resurrected the use of the word <i>cosmos</i> from the ancient Greek and assigned it to his multi-volume treatise, <i><a href="/wiki/Kosmos_(Humboldt)" title="Kosmos (Humboldt)">Kosmos</a></i>, in which he sought to unify diverse branches of scientific knowledge and culture. This important work also motivated a holistic perception of the universe as one interacting entity.<sup id="cite_ref-Walls_2009_3.E2.80.9315_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walls_2009_3.E2.80.9315-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Other_aspects_of_Humboldt.27s_life_and_career"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Other aspects of Humboldt's life and career</span></a>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography_of_early_life">Biography of early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography of early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Tegel1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Schloss_Tegel1.JPG/220px-Schloss_Tegel1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Schloss_Tegel1.JPG/330px-Schloss_Tegel1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Schloss_Tegel1.JPG/440px-Schloss_Tegel1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Tegel1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Tegel Palace, Berlin, where Alexander and <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">his brother Wilhelm</a> lived for several years.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg/220px-Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg/330px-Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg/440px-Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3138" data-file-height="2382" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexander_von_Humboldt_and_Mother.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humboldt as a boy with his widowed mother, Maria Elisabeth (Colomb) von Humboldt</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alexander von Humboldt was born in Berlin in <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> on 14 September 1769.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-11">[11]</a></sup> He was baptized as a baby in the Lutheran faith, with the Duke of Brunswick serving as godfather.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19553_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19553-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt's father, Alexander Georg von Humboldt, belonged to a prominent <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomeranian</a> family, although not one of the titled gentry; a major in the <a href="/wiki/Prussian_Army" title="Prussian Army">Prussian Army</a>, who had served with the Duke of Brunswick.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19554-5_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19554-5-13">[13]</a></sup> At age 42, Alexander Georg was rewarded for his services in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> with the post of Royal <a href="/wiki/Chamberlain_(office)" title="Chamberlain (office)">Chamberlain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup> He profited from the contract to lease state lotteries and tobacco sales.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19555_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19555-15">[15]</a></sup> He first married the daughter of Prussian General Adjutant Schweder.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1766, Alexander Georg married Maria Elisabeth Colomb, a well-educated woman and widow of Baron Hollwede, with whom she had a son. Alexander Georg and Maria Elisabeth had three children, a daughter, who died young, and then two sons, Wilhelm and Alexander. Her first-born son, Wilhelm's and Alexander's half-brother, was something of a ne'er do well, not often mentioned in the family history.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19556-7_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra19556-7-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Alexander Georg died in 1779, leaving the brothers Humboldt in the care of their emotionally distant mother. She did have high ambitions for Alexander and his older brother Wilhelm, hiring excellent tutors, who were <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Enlightenment</a> thinkers, including Kantian physician <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Herz" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcus Herz">Marcus Herz</a> and botanist <a href="/wiki/Karl_Ludwig_Willdenow" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl Ludwig Willdenow">Karl Ludwig Willdenow</a>, who became one of the most important botanists in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi-17">[17]</a></sup>Humboldt's mother expected them to become civil servants of the Prussian state.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201513.2C_17_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201513.2C_17-18">[18]</a></sup> The money Baron Holwede left to Alexander's mother became, after her death, instrumental in funding Alexander's explorations, contributing more than 70% of his private income.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Due to his youthful penchant for collecting and labeling plants, shells and insects, Alexander received the playful title of "the little apothecary".<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup> Marked for a political career, Alexander studied <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a> for six months in 1787 at the <a href="/wiki/Viadrina_European_University" title="Viadrina European University">University of Frankfurt (Oder)</a>, which his mother might have chosen less for its academic excellence as its closeness to their home in Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201517_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201517-19">[19]</a></sup> On April 25, 1789, he matriculated at <a href="/wiki/University_of_G%C3%B6ttingen" title="University of Göttingen">Göttingen</a>, then known for the lectures of <a href="/wiki/Christian_Gottlob_Heine" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Gottlob Heine">C. G. Heyne</a> and anatomist <a href="/wiki/Johann_Friedrich_Blumenbach" title="Johann Friedrich Blumenbach">J. F. Blumenbach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi-17">[17]</a></sup> His brother Wilhelm was already a student at Göttingen, but they did not interact much since their intellectual interests were quite different.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201518_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201518-20">[20]</a></sup> His vast and varied interests were by this time fully developed.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Göttingen he met <a href="/wiki/Georg_Forster" title="Georg Forster">Georg Forster</a>, a naturalist who had been with Captain <a href="/wiki/James_Cook" title="James Cook">James Cook</a> on his second voyage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi-xv_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xvi-xv-21">[21]</a></sup> Humboldt traveled with Forster in Europe. The two traveled to England, Humboldt's first sea voyage, The Netherlands, and France.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201518_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201518-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xv_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xv-22">[22]</a></sup> In England, he met Sir <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Banks" title="Joseph Banks">Joseph Banks</a>, President of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a>, who had traveled with Captain Cook; Banks showed Humboldt his huge herbarium, with specimens of the South Sea tropics.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xv_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENicolson1995xv-22">[22]</a></sup> The scientific friendship between Banks and Humboldt lasted until Banks's death in 1820, and the two shared botanical specimens for study. Banks also mobilized his scientific contacts in later years to aid Humboldt's work.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201576.2C_136_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201576.2C_136-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt's scientific excursion up the <a href="/wiki/Rhine" title="Rhine">Rhine</a> resulted in his 1790 treatise <i>Mineralogische Beobachtungen über einige Basalte am Rhein</i> (Brunswick, 1790)<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup> (<i>Mineralogic Observations on Several Basalts on the River Rhine</i>).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandre_humboldt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexandre_humboldt.jpg/170px-Alexandre_humboldt.jpg" width="170" height="235" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexandre_humboldt.jpg/255px-Alexandre_humboldt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Alexandre_humboldt.jpg/340px-Alexandre_humboldt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1655" data-file-height="2288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alexandre_humboldt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of Alexander von Humboldt by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Georg_Weitsch" title="Friedrich Georg Weitsch">Friedrich Georg Weitsch</a>, 1806</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Humboldt's passion for travel was of long standing. Humboldt's talents were devoted to the purpose of preparing himself as a scientific explorer. With this emphasis, he studied commerce and foreign languages at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hamburg" title="University of Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, geology at <a href="/wiki/Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Bergakademie_Freiberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Technische Universität Bergakademie Freiberg">Technische Universität Bergakademie Freiberg</a> in 1791 under <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Gottlob_Werner" title="Abraham Gottlob Werner">A.G. Werner</a>, leader of the <a href="/wiki/Neptunist" class="mw-redirect" title="Neptunist">Neptunist</a> school of geology;<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> from anatomy at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Jena" title="University of Jena">Jena</a> under <a href="/wiki/Justus_Christian_Loder" title="Justus Christian Loder">J.C. Loder</a>; and astronomy and the use of scientific instruments under <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_von_Zach" title="Franz Xaver von Zach">F.X. von Zach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johann_Gottfried_Koehler" title="Johann Gottfried Koehler">J.G. Köhler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup> At Freiberg, he met a number of men who were to prove important to him in his later career, including Spaniard Manuel del Rio, who became director of the School of Mines the crown established in Mexico; <a href="/wiki/Christian_Leopold_von_Buch" title="Christian Leopold von Buch">Christian Leopold von Buch</a>, who became a regional geologist; and, most importantly, Karl Freiesleben, who became Humboldt's tutor and close friend. During this period, his brother Wilhelm married, but Alexander did not attend the nuptials.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195551_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195551-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Travels_and_work_in_Europe">Travels and work in Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Travels and work in Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Humboldt graduated from the <a href="/wiki/Freiberg_University_of_Mining_and_Technology" title="Freiberg University of Mining and Technology">Freiberg School of Mines</a> in 1792 and was appointed to a Prussian government position in the Department of Mines as an inspector in Bayreuth and the Fichtel mountains. Humboldt was excellent at his job, with production of gold ore in his first year outstripping the previous eight years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195553_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195553-26">[26]</a></sup> During his period as a mine inspector, Humboldt demonstrated his deep concern for the men laboring in the mines. He opened a free school for miners, paid for out of his own pocket, which became an unchartered government training school for labor. He also sought to establish an emergency relief fund for miners, aiding them following accidents.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195554-55_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195554-55-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt's researches into the vegetation of the mines of <a href="/wiki/Freiberg,_Saxony" class="mw-redirect" title="Freiberg, Saxony">Freiberg</a> led to the publication in Latin (1793) of his <i>Florae Fribergensis, accedunt Aphorismi ex Doctrina, Physiologiae Chemicae Plantarum</i>, which was a compendium of his botantical researches.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> That publication brought him to the attention of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_von_Goethe" title="Johann Wolfgang von Goethe">Johann Wolfgang von Goethe</a>, who had met Humboldt at the family home when Alexander was a boy, but Goethe was now interested in meeting the young scientist in order to discuss metamorphism of plants.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195518.2C_57_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195518.2C_57-29">[29]</a></sup> An introduction was arranged by Humboldt's brother who lived in the university town of Jena, not far from Goethe. Goethe had developed his own extensive theories on comparative anatomy. Working before Darwin, he believed that animals had an internal force, an <i>urform</i>, that gave them a basic shape and then they were further adapted to their environment by an external force. Humboldt urged him to publish his theories. Together the two discussed and expanded these ideas. Goethe and Humboldt soon became close friends.</p>
<p>Humboldt would often return to Jena in the years that followed. Goethe remarked about Humboldt to friends that he had never met someone so versatile. Humboldt's drive served as an inspiration for Goethe. In 1797, Humboldt returned to Jena for three months. During this time Goethe moved from his residence in Weimar to reside in Jena. Together Humboldt and Goethe would attend university lectures on anatomy and conduct their own experiments. One experiment involved hooking up a frog leg to various metals. They found no effect until the moisture of Humboldt's breath triggered a reaction that caused the frog leg to leap off the table. Humboldt would describe this as one of his favorite experiments because it was as if he was "breathing life into" the leg.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf2015_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf2015-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>During this visit, a thunderstorm killed a farmer and his wife. Humboldt obtained their corpses and analyzed them in the anatomy tower of the university.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf2015_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf2015-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Weimarer_Klassik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Weimarer_Klassik.jpg/220px-Weimarer_Klassik.jpg" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Weimarer_Klassik.jpg/330px-Weimarer_Klassik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Weimarer_Klassik.jpg/440px-Weimarer_Klassik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="657" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Weimarer_Klassik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Schiller, Wilhelm and Alexander von Humboldt with Goethe in <a href="/wiki/Jena" title="Jena">Jena</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1794 Humboldt was admitted to the famous group of intellectuals and cultural leaders of <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Classicism" title="Weimar Classicism">Weimar Classicism</a>. Goethe and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller" title="Friedrich Schiller">Schiller</a> were the key figures at the time. Humboldt contributed (7 June 1795) to Schiller's new periodical, <i>Die Horen</i>, a philosophical <a href="/wiki/Allegory" title="Allegory">allegory</a> entitled <i>Die Lebenskraft, oder der rhodische Genius</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1792 and 1797 Humboldt was in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>; in 1795 he made a geological and botanical tour through Switzerland and Italy. Although this service to the state was regarded by him as only an apprenticeship to the service of science, he fulfilled its duties with such conspicuous ability that not only did he rise rapidly to the highest post in his department, but he was also entrusted with several important diplomatic missions.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>The death of his stern mother, on 19 November 1796 after a year's suffering with cancer, set him free. Neither brother attended the funeral.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201539_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201539-31">[31]</a></sup> Humboldt had not hidden his aversion to his mother, with one correspondent writing him after her death, "her death...must be particularly welcomed by you."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> After severing his official connections, he awaited an opportunity to fulfill his long-cherished dream of travel.</p>
<p>Humboldt was able to spend more time on writing up his research. He had used his own body for experimentation on muscular irritability, recently discovered by <a href="/wiki/Luigi_Galvani" title="Luigi Galvani">Luigi Galvani</a> and published his results, <i>Versuche über die gereizte Muskel- und Nervenfaser</i> (Berlin, 1797) (<i>Experiments on Stimulated Muscle and Nerve Fibres</i>), enriched in the French translation with notes by Blumenbach.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_American_expedition.2C_1799.E2.80.931804">Spanish American expedition, 1799–1804</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Spanish American expedition, 1799–1804">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg/220px-Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg.png" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg/330px-Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg/440px-Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2844" data-file-height="1903" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_Alexander_von_Humboldt_expedition-en.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alexander von Humboldt's Latin American expedition</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seeking_a_foreign_expedition">Seeking a foreign expedition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Seeking a foreign expedition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the financial resources to finance his scientific travels, he sought a ship on a major expedition. Meantime, he went to Paris where his brother Wilhelm was now living. Paris was a great center of scientific learning and his brother and sister-in-law Caroline were well connected in those circles. <a href="/wiki/Louis-Antoine_de_Bougainville" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-Antoine de Bougainville">Louis-Antoine de Bougainville</a> urged Humboldt to accompany him on a major expedition, likely to last five years, but the French revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Directoire" class="mw-redirect" title="Directoire">Directoire</a> placed <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Baudin" title="Nicolas Baudin">Nicolas Baudin</a> at the head of it rather than the aging scientific traveler.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195580_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195580-33">[33]</a></sup> On the postponement of Captain Baudin's proposed voyage of <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">circumnavigation</a> due to continuing warfare in Europe, which Humboldt had been officially invited to accompany, Humboldt was deeply disappointed. He had already selected scientific instruments for his voyage. He did, however, have a stroke of luck with meeting <a href="/wiki/Aim%C3%A9_Bonpland" title="Aimé Bonpland">Aimé Bonpland</a>, the botanist and physician for the voyage. Discouraged, the two left Paris for <a href="/wiki/Marseilles" class="mw-redirect" title="Marseilles">Marseilles</a>, where they hoped to join <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> in Egypt. But North Africans were in revolt against the French invasion in Egypt and French authorities refused permission to travel. Humboldt and Bonpland eventually found their way to <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, where their luck changed spectacularly.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_royal_authorization_1799">Spanish royal authorization 1799</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Spanish royal authorization 1799">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg/220px-Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg" width="220" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg/330px-Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg/440px-Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2240" data-file-height="3051" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlos_IV_de_rojo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV of Spain</a> who authorized Humboldt's travels and research in Spanish America</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Madrid, Humboldt sought authorization to travel to Spain's realms in the Americas; he was aided in obtaining it by the German representative of Saxony at the royal Bourbon court. Baron Forell had an interest in mineralogy and science endeavors and inclined to help Humboldt.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583-34">[34]</a></sup> Humboldt's timing could not have been better to interest the Spanish crown in an extended scientific expedition to their possessions in the New World. With the accession of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">House of Bourbon</a> to the Spanish throne following the death of the last Hapsburg king, Charles II (d. 1700), and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, which the House of Bourbon won, the Spanish Bourbons embarked on a program of reform in Spain and then Spanish America. The <a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Reforms" title="Bourbon Reforms">Bourbon Reforms</a> sought to reform administration of the realms and revitalize their economies.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> At the same time as the Bourbon reforms, the Spanish Enlightenment was in fluorescence. For Humboldt, "the confluent effect of the Bourbon revolution in government and the Spanish Enlightenment had created ideal conditions for his venture."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Bourbon monarchy had already authorized and funded expeditions, with the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_Expedition_to_the_Viceroyalty_of_Peru" title="Botanical Expedition to the Viceroyalty of Peru">Botanical Expedition to the Viceroyalty of Peru</a> to Chile and Peru (1777–88), New Granada (1783–1816), New Spain (Mexico) (1787–1803), and the <a href="/wiki/Malaspina_Expedition" title="Malaspina Expedition">Malaspina Expedition</a> (1789–94). These were lengthy, state-sponsored enterprises to gather information about plants and animals from the Spanish realms, assess economic possibilities, and provide plants and seeds for the Royal Botanical Garden in Madrid (founded 1755).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBleichmar20125_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBleichmar20125-37">[37]</a></sup> These expeditions took naturalists and artists, who created visual images as well as careful written observations as well as collecting seeds and plants themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBleichmar201219_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBleichmar201219-38">[38]</a></sup> Crown officials as early as 1779 issued and systematically distributed <i>Instructions concerning the most secure and economic means to transport live plants by land and sea from the most distant countries</i>, with illustrations, including one for the crates to transport seeds and plants.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Humboldt requested authorization from the crown to travel to Spanish America, most importantly, with his own financing, it was given positive response. Spain under the Hapsburg monarchy had guarded its realms against foreigner travelers and intruders. The Bourbon monarch was open to Humboldt's proposal. Spanish Foreign Minister Don <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Luis_de_Urquijo" title="Mariano Luis de Urquijo">Mariano Luis de Urquijo</a> received the formal proposal and Humboldt was presented to the monarch in March 1799.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195583-34">[34]</a></sup> Humboldt was granted access to crown officials and written documentation on Spain's empire. With Humboldt's experience working for the absolutist Prussian monarchy as a government mining official, Humboldt had both the academic training and experience of working well within a bureaucratic structure.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before leaving Madrid in 1799, Humboldt and Bonpland visited the Natural History Museum which held results of <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_de_Sess%C3%A9_y_Lacasta" class="mw-redirect" title="Martín de Sessé y Lacasta">Martín de Sessé y Lacasta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mariano_Moci%C3%B1o" title="José Mariano Mociño">José Mariano Mociño</a>'s botanical expedition to <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Humboldt and Bonpland met <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lito_Ruiz_L%C3%B3pez" title="Hipólito Ruiz López">Hipólito Ruiz López</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Pav%C3%B3n_y_Jim%C3%A9nez" class="mw-redirect" title="José Antonio Pavón y Jiménez">José Antonio Pavón y Jiménez</a> of the royal expedition to Peru and Chile in person in Madrid and examined their botanical collections.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela_1799.E2.80.931800">Venezuela 1799–1800</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Venezuela 1799–1800">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg/220px-Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg/330px-Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg/440px-Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="401" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt_and_Bonplant_in_the_Jungle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humboldt and Bonpland in the Amazon rainforest by the Casiquiare River, with their scientific instruments, which enabled them to take many types of accurate measurements throughout their five-year journey. Oil painting by <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Ender" title="Eduard Ender">Eduard Ender</a>, 1856.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg/200px-Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg" width="200" height="307" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg/300px-Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg/400px-Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1308" data-file-height="2011" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Canal_do_Cassiquiare.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the Cassiquiare canal based on Humboldt's 1799 observations.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Armed with authorization from the King of Spain, Humboldt and Bonpland made haste to sail, taking the ship <i>Pizarro</i> from <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">A Coruña</a>, on 5 June 1799. The ship stopped six days on the island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, where Humboldt climbed the volcano <a href="/wiki/Teide" title="Teide">Teide</a>, and then sailed on to the New World, landing at <a href="/wiki/Cuman%C3%A1" title="Cumaná">Cumaná</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, on 16 July.</p>
<p>The ship's destination was not originally Cumaná, but an outbreak of typhoid on board so that the captain changed course from <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a> to land in northern South America. Humboldt had not mapped out a specific plan of exploration, so that the change did not upend a fixed itinerary. He later wrote that the diversion to Venezuela made possible his explorations along the Orinoco River to the border of Portuguese Brazil. With the diversion, the <i>Pizarro</i> encounter two large dugout canoes each carrying 18 Guayaqui Indians. The <i>Pizarro'</i>s, captain accepted the offer of one of them to serve as pilot. Humboldt hired this Indian, named Carlos del Pino, as a guide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195591-92_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra195591-92-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>Venezuela from the sixteenth century to the eighteenth was a relative backwater compared to the seats of the Spanish viceroyalties based in New Spain (Mexico) and Peru, but during the Bourbon reforms, the northern portion of Spanish South America was reorganized administratively, with the 1777 establishment of a Captaincy-General based at Caracas. A great deal of information on the new jurisdiction had already been compiled by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Pons&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="François de Pons (page does not exist)">François de Pons</a> and published in 1806.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrading1991517-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Rather than describe the administrative center of Caracas, Humboldt started his researches with the valley of Aragua where export crops of sugar, coffee, cacao, and cotton were cultivated. Cacao plantations were the most profitable as world demand for chocolate rose.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrading1991518_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrading1991518-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt visited the mission at <a href="/wiki/Caripe" title="Caripe">Caripe</a> and explored the <a href="/wiki/Cueva_del_Gu%C3%A1charo_National_Park" title="Cueva del Guácharo National Park">Guácharo cavern</a>, where he found the <a href="/wiki/Oilbird" title="Oilbird">oilbird</a>, which he was to make known to science as <i>Steatornis caripensis</i>. Also described the <a href="/wiki/Lake_Bermudez" title="Lake Bermudez">Guanoco</a> asphalt lake as "The spring of the good priest" ("<i>Quelle des guten Priesters</i>").<sup id="cite_ref-G_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-G-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-H_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-H-46">[46]</a></sup> Returning to Cumaná, Humboldt observed, on the night of 11–12 November, a remarkable <a href="/wiki/Meteor_shower" title="Meteor shower">meteor shower</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Leonids" title="Leonids">Leonids</a>). He proceeded with Bonpland to <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a> where he climbed the <a href="/wiki/El_%C3%81vila_National_Park" title="El Ávila National Park">Avila mount</a> with the young poet <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bello" title="Andrés Bello">Andrés Bello</a>, the former tutor of <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a>, who later became the leader of independence in northern South America. Humboldt met the Venezuelan Bolívar himself in 1804 in Paris and spent time with him in Rome. The documentary record does not support the supposition that Humboldt inspired Bolívar to participate in the struggle for independence, but it does indicate Bolívar's admiration for Humboldt's production of new knowledge on Spanish America.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955232-33_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955232-33-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 1800, Humboldt and Bonpland left the coast with the purpose of exploring the course of the <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a> and its tributaries. This trip, which lasted four months and covered 1,725 miles (2,776&#160;km) of wild and largely uninhabited country, had the important result of establishing the existence of the <a href="/wiki/Casiquiare_canal" title="Casiquiare canal">Casiquiare canal</a> (a communication between the water-systems of the rivers Orinoco and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">Amazon</a>), and of determining the exact position of the <a href="/wiki/River_bifurcation" title="River bifurcation">bifurcation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup> as well as documenting the life of several native tribes such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Maypure&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Maypure (page does not exist)">Maipures</a> and their extinct rivals the Atures (several words of the latter tribe were transferred to Humboldt by one parrot<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>). Around 19 March 1800, Humboldt and Bonpland discovered dangerous <a href="/wiki/Electric_eel" title="Electric eel">electric eels</a>, whose shock could kill a man. To catch them, locals suggested they drive wild horses into the river, which brought the eels out from the river mud, and resulted in a violent confrontation of eels and horses, some of which died. Humboldt and Bonpland captured and dissected some eels, which retained their ability to shock; both received potentially dangerous electric shocks during their investigations. The encounter made Humboldt think more deeply about electricity and magnetism, typical of his ability to extrapolate from an observation more general principles.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Humboldt returned to the incident in several of his later writings, including his travelogue <i>Personal Narrative</i> (1814–29), <i>Views of Nature</i> (1807), and <i>Aspects of Nature</i> (1849).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two months later they explored the territory of the Maypures and that of the then recently extinct Aturès Indians. Humboldt laid to rest the persistent myth of <a href="/wiki/Walter_Raleigh" title="Walter Raleigh">Walter Raleigh</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lake_Parime" title="Lake Parime">Lake Parime</a> by proposing that the seasonal flooding of the <a href="/wiki/Rupununi_savannah" title="Rupununi savannah">Rupununi savannah</a> had been misidentified as a lake.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuba_1800.2C_1804">Cuba 1800, 1804</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cuba 1800, 1804">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg/220px-Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg" width="220" height="272" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg/330px-Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg/440px-Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="460" data-file-height="569" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chiranthodendron_pentadactylon_monochrome.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humboldt botanical drawing published in his work on Cuba</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 24 November 1800, the two friends set sail for Cuba, landing on December 19,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> where they met fellow botanist and <a href="/wiki/Plant_collector" class="mw-redirect" title="Plant collector">plant collector</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Fraser_(botanist)" title="John Fraser (botanist)">John Fraser</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brendel_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brendel-53">[53]</a></sup> Fraser and his son had been shipwrecked off the Cuban coast, and did not have a license to be in the Spanish Indies. Humboldt, who was already in Cuba, interceded with crown officials in Havana, as well as giving them money and clothing. Fraser obtained permission to remain in Cuba and explore. Humboldt entrusted Fraser with taking two cases of Humboldt and Bonpland's botanical specimens to England when he returned, for eventual conveyance to the German botantist Willdenow in Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955116-17_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955116-17-54">[54]</a></sup> Humboldt and Bonpland stayed in Cuba until March 5, 1801, when they left for the mainland of northern South America again on March 30, 1801.</p>
<p>Humboldt is considered to be the "second discoverer of Cuba" due to the scientific and social research he conducted on this Spanish colony. During an initial three-month stay at <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, his first tasks were to properly survey that city and the nearby towns of <a href="/wiki/Guanabacoa" title="Guanabacoa">Guanabacoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regla" title="Regla">Regla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bejucal" title="Bejucal">Bejucal</a>. He befriended Cuban landowner and thinker <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Arango_y_Parre%C3%B1o" title="Francisco de Arango y Parreño">Francisco de Arango y Parreño</a>; together they visited the <span lang="spa" xml:lang="spa">Guines</span> area in south Havana, the valleys of <a href="/wiki/Matanzas" title="Matanzas">Matanzas</a> Province and the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_the_Sugar_Mills" class="mw-redirect" title="Valley of the Sugar Mills">Valley of the Sugar Mills</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Cuba" title="Trinidad, Cuba">Trinidad</a>. Those three areas were, at the time, the first frontier of sugar production in the island. During those trips, Humboldt collected statistical information on Cuba's population, production, technology and trade, and with Arango, made suggestions for enhancing them. He predicted that the agricultural and commercial potential of Cuba was huge and could be vastly improved with proper leadership in the future.</p>
<p>On their way back to Europe from Mexico on their way to the United States, Humboldt and Bonpland stopped again in Cuba, leaving from the port of Veracruz and arriving in Cuba on January 7, 1804 staying until April 29, 1804. In Cuba, he collected material plant material and made extensive notes. During his time he socialized with his scientific and landowner friends, conducted mineralogical surveys and finished his vast collection of the island's flora and fauna that he eventually published as <i>Essai politique sur l'îsle de Cuba</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Andes_1801.E2.80.931803">The Andes 1801–1803</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Andes 1801–1803">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg/350px-Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg" width="350" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg/525px-Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="360" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Humboldt-Bonpland_Chimborazo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humboldt and his fellow scientist Aimé Bonpland at the foot of the Chimborazo volcano, painting by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Georg_Weitsch" title="Friedrich Georg Weitsch">Friedrich Georg Weitsch</a> (1810).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After their first stay in Cuba of three months they returned the mainland at <a href="/wiki/Cartagena_de_Indias" class="mw-redirect" title="Cartagena de Indias">Cartagena de Indias</a> (now in Colombia), a major center of trade in northern South America. Ascending the swollen stream of the <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_River" title="Magdalena River">Magdalena River</a> to Honda and arrived in Bogotá on July 6, 1801 where they met Spanish botanist <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis" title="José Celestino Mutis">José Celestino Mutis</a>, the head of the Royal Botanical Expedition to New Granada, staying there until September 8, 1801. Mutis was generous with his time and gave Humboldt access to the huge pictorial record he had compiled since 1783. Mutis was based in Bogotá, but as with other Spanish expeditions, he had access to local knowledge and a workshop of artists, who created highly accurate and detailed images. This type of careful recording meant that even if specimens were not available to study at a distance, "because the images traveled, the botanists did not have to."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBleichmar2012190_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBleichmar2012190-56">[56]</a></sup> Humboldt was astounded at Mutis's accomplishment; when Humboldt published his first volume on botany, he dedicated it to Mutis, "as a simply mark of our admiration and acknowledgement."<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/220px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/330px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg/440px-Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ilustraciones_Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Illustrations from Spanish botanist <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Celestino_Mutis" title="José Celestino Mutis">José Celestino Mutis</a>'s work in Colombia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Humboldt had hopes of connecting with the French sailing expedition of Baudin, now finally underway, so Bonpland and Humboldt hurried to Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-55">[55]</a></sup> They crossed the frozen ridges of the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Real_(Ecuador)" title="Cordillera Real (Ecuador)">Cordillera Real</a>, they reached <a href="/wiki/Quito" title="Quito">Quito</a> on 6 January 1802, after a tedious and difficult journey.</p>
<p>Their stay in Ecuador was marked by the ascent of <a href="/wiki/Pichincha_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pichincha (volcano)">Pichincha</a> and their climb of <a href="/wiki/Chimborazo_(volcano)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chimborazo (volcano)">Chimborazo</a>, where Humboldt and his party reached an altitude of 19,286 feet (5,878&#160;m). This was a world record at the time, but a thousand feet short of the summit.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Humboldt's journey concluded with an expedition to the sources of the Amazon <i>en route</i> for <a href="/wiki/Lima,_Peru" class="mw-redirect" title="Lima, Peru">Lima, Peru</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Callao" title="Callao">Callao</a>, the main port for Peru, Humboldt observed the <a href="/wiki/Transit_of_Mercury" title="Transit of Mercury">transit of Mercury</a>. On 9 November and studied the fertilizing properties of <a href="/wiki/Guano" title="Guano">guano</a>, rich in nitrogen, the subsequent introduction of which into Europe was due mainly to his writings.<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico_1803.E2.80.9304">Mexico 1803–04</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mexico 1803–04">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MINA_GTO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MINA_GTO.jpg/220px-MINA_GTO.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MINA_GTO.jpg/330px-MINA_GTO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MINA_GTO.jpg/440px-MINA_GTO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1661" data-file-height="1160" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MINA_GTO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Silver mining complex of La Valenciana, Guanajuato, Mexico</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res,_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_(1813)_(14781309784).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg/200px-Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg/300px-Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg/400px-Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res%2C_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_%281813%29_%2814781309784%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1093" data-file-height="1642" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vues_des_Cordill%C3%A8res,_et_monumens_des_peuples_indig%C3%A8nes_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique_(1813)_(14781309784).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne,_sog._Aztekenkalender,_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG/250px-1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG" width="250" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG/375px-1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG/500px-1479_Stein_der_f%C3%BCnften_Sonne%2C_sog._Aztekenkalender%2C_Ollin_Tonatiuh_anagoria.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4750" data-file-height="4064" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
