<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_aspects_of_Humboldt.27s_life_and_career">Other aspects of Humboldt's life and career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Other aspects of Humboldt's life and career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humboldt_and_the_Prussian_monarchy">Humboldt and the Prussian monarchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Humboldt and the Prussian monarchy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg/170px-AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg" width="170" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg/255px-AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg/340px-AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="703" data-file-height="693" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AlexanderVonHumboldtBriefsiegel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Humboldt's <a href="/wiki/Seal_(emblem)" title="Seal (emblem)">seal</a> on a private letter</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the Napoleonic wars, Prussia had capitulated to France, signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tilsit" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Tilsit">Treaty of Tilsit</a>. The Prussian royal family returned to Berlin, but sought better terms of the treaty and Friedrich Wilhelm III commissioned his younger brother Prince Wilhelm with this. Friedrich Wilhelm III asked Alexander to be part of the mission, charged with introducing the prince to Paris society. This turn of events for Humboldt could not have been better, since he desired to live in Paris rather than Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955210_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955210-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1814 Humboldt accompanied the allied sovereigns to London. Three years later he was summoned by the king of Prussia to attend him at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1818)" title="Congress of Aix-la-Chapelle (1818)">congress of Aachen</a>. Again in the autumn of 1822 he accompanied the same monarch to the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Verona" title="Congress of Verona">Congress of Verona</a>, proceeded thence with the royal party to Rome and Naples and returned to Paris in the spring of 1823. Humboldt had long regarded Paris as his true home. Thus, when at last he received from his sovereign a summons to join his court at Berlin, he obeyed reluctantly.</p>
<p>Between 1830 and 1848 Humboldt was frequently employed in diplomatic missions to the court of <a href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-Philippe of France">King Louis Philippe</a> of France, with whom he always maintained the most cordial personal relations. Charles X of France had been overthrown, with Louis-Philippe of the house of Orléan becoming king. Humboldt knew the family, and he was sent by the Prussian monarch to Paris to report on events to his monarch. He spent three years in France, from 1830 to 1833. His friends <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Arago" title="François Arago">François Arago</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Guizot" class="mw-redirect" title="Guillaume Guizot">Guillaume Guizot</a>, who were appointed to posts in Louis-Philippe's government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955311_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955311-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt's brother, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm</a>, died on 8 April 1835. Alexander lamented that he had lost half of himself with the death of his brother. Upon the accession of the crown prince <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_IV_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William IV of Prussia">Frederick William IV</a> in June 1840, Humboldt's favor at court increased. Indeed, the new king's craving for Humboldt's company became at times so importunate as to leave him only a few waking hours to work on his writing.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because Humboldt did not mention God in his work <i>Cosmos</i>, and sometimes spoke unfavourably of hypocritical religious attitudes, it was occasionally speculated that he was a materialist philosopher, or perhaps an atheist.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> However, unlike irreligious figures such as <a href="/wiki/Robert_G._Ingersoll" title="Robert G. Ingersoll">Robert G. Ingersoll</a>, who went so far as to use Humboldtian science to campaign against religion,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Humboldt himself denied imputations of atheism. In a letter to <a href="/wiki/Karl_August_Varnhagen_von_Ense" title="Karl August Varnhagen von Ense">Varnhagen von Ense</a> he emphasized that he believed the world had indeed been created, writing of <i>Cosmos</i>: "...'creation' and the 'created world' are never lost sight of in the book. And did I not, only eight months ago, in the French translation, say, in the plainest terms: 'It is this necessity of things, this occult but permanent connection, this periodical return in the progress, development of formation, phenomena, and events which constitute 'Nature' submissive to a controlling power?'"<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<p>It has been argued that "although Humboldt emphasizes the basis of morality in the nature of man, he does acknowledge that a belief in God is linked directly to acts of virtue" and therefore "the dignity of man lies at the centre of Humboldt's religious thought."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt also believed firmly in an <a href="/wiki/Afterlife" title="Afterlife">afterlife</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> A letter he wrote to his friend Charlotte Hildebrand Diede states: "God constantly appoints the course of nature and of circumstances; so that, including his existence in an eternal future, the happiness of the individual does not perish, but on the contrary grows and increases."<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt remained distant of organized religion: he did not believe in the Bible as an <a href="/wiki/Biblical_inerrancy" title="Biblical inerrancy">inerrant</a> document, nor in the divinity of Jesus; yet, Humboldt still held deep respect for the ideal side of religious belief and church life within human communities.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> He differentiated between "negative" religions, and those "all positive religions [which] consist of three distinct parts — a code of morals which is nearly the same in all of them, and generally very pure; a geological chimera, and a myth or a little historical novel."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> In <i>Cosmos</i>, he wrote about how rich geological descriptions were found in different religious traditions, and stated:"Christianity gradually diffused itself, and, wherever it was adopted as the religion of the state, it not only exercised a beneficial condition on the lower classes by inculcating the social freedom of mankind, but also expanded the views of men in their communion with Nature...this tendency to glorify the Deity in his works gave rise to a taste for natural observation."|<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt showed <a href="/wiki/Religious_tolerance" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious tolerance">religious tolerance</a> towards Judaism, and he criticized the political <i>Jews Bill</i>, which was an initiative intended to establish legal discrimination against Jews. He called this an "abominable" law, since he hoped to see Jews being treated equally in society.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin,_Oranienburger_Str._67_(Gem%C3%A4lde).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg/220px-Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg/330px-Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg/440px-Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin%2C_Oranienburger_Str._67_%28Gem%C3%A4lde%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4628" data-file-height="3049" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arbeitszimmer_des_Alexander_von_Humboldt_in_Berlin,_Oranienburger_Str._67_(Gem%C3%A4lde).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alexander von Humboldt in his library in his Oranienburger Strasse, Berlin apartment, by <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Hildebrandt" title="Eduard Hildebrandt">Eduard Hildebrandt</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg/170px-Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg" width="170" height="197" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg/255px-Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg/340px-Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3140" data-file-height="3638" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baron_Alexander_von_Humboldt_by_Julius_Schrader_1859.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portrait of Humboldt by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Schrader" title="Julius Schrader">Julius Schrader</a>, 1859. <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Art" title="Metropolitan Museum of Art">Metropolitan Museum of Art</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Much of Humboldt's private life remains a mystery because he destroyed his private letters. While a gregarious personality, he may have harbored a sense of social alienation, which drove his passion for escape through travel.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESachs200764_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESachs200764-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt never married: while he was charmed by a number of attractive women, including Henriette, the wife of his mentor Marcus Herz, his sister-in-law Caroline von Humboldt stated "nothing will ever have a great influence on Alexander that doesn't come through men."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201571_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201571-180">[180]</a></sup> He had many strong male friendships, and at times had romances with men.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESachs200765_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESachs200765-181">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a student he became infatuated with Wilhelm Gabriel Wegener, a theology student, penning a succession of letters expressing his "fervent love".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelferich20048_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelferich20048-182">[182]</a></sup> At 25 he met Reinhardt von Haeften, a 21 year old lieutenant, with whom he lived and travelled with for two years, and to whom he wrote in 1794: "I only live through you, my good precious Reinhardt." When von Haeften became engaged, Humboldt begged to remain living with him and his wife: "Even if you must refuse me, treat me coldly with disdain, I should still want to be with you...the love I have for you is not just friendship or brotherly love, it is veneration"<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERupke2008187-200_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupke2008187-200-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<p>A travelling companion in the Americas for five years was Aimé Bonpland, and in Quito in 1802 he met the Ecuadorian aristocrat Don Carlos Montúfar, who travelled with Humboldt to Europe and lived with him. In France, Humboldt travelled and lived with the physicist and balloonist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Louis_Gay_Lussac" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Louis Gay Lussac">Joseph Louis Gay Lussac</a>. Later he had a deep friendship with the married French astronomer <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Arago" title="François Arago">François Arago</a>, whom he met daily for 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt once wrote "I don't know sensual needs."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf201571_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf201571-180">[180]</a></sup> However, a pious travelling companion, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jos%C3%A9_de_Caldas" title="Francisco José de Caldas">Francisco José de Caldas</a>, accused him of frequenting houses in Quito where "impure love reigned", of making friends with "obscene dissolute youths", of giving vent to "shameful passions of his heart", and dropping him to travel with "Bonpland and his Adonis"[Monúfar].<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Humboldt inherited a significant fortune, but the expense of his travels, and most especially of publishing (thirty volumes in all), had by 1834 made him totally reliant on the pension of King Frederick William III.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalls2009109_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalls2009109-186">[186]</a></sup> Although he preferred living in Paris, by 1836 the King had insisted he return to Germany. He lived with the Court at <a href="/wiki/Sanssouci" title="Sanssouci">Sanssouci</a>, and latterly in Berlin, with his valet Seifert, who had accompanied him to Russia in 1829.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955363_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955363-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg/220px-SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg.png" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg/330px-SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg/440px-SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="554" data-file-height="276" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SignaturAlexanderVonHumboldt.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Signature of Humboldt late in life, when his handwriting became increasingly difficult to read</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Four years before his death, Humboldt executed a deed of gift transferring his entire estate to the dominating Seifert,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalls2009367_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalls2009367-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHelferich2004312_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHelferich2004312-189">[189]</a></sup> who had by then married and set up a household near Humboldt's apartment. Humboldt had become godfather to his daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955317_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955317-190">[190]</a></sup> The scale of the bequest has always drawn speculation, especially as Seifert was some thirty years younger, and introducing lower class partners into households under the guise of servants was then a common practice.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1908, the sexual researcher <a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_N%C3%A4cke" class="extiw" title="de:Paul Näcke">Paul Näcke</a> gathered reminiscences from homosexuals<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> including Humboldt's friend the botanist Karl Bolle, then 90 years old: some of the material was incorporated by <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Hirschfeld" title="Magnus Hirschfeld">Magnus Hirschfeld</a> into his 1914 study <i>Homosexuality in Men and Women.</i><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> However, speculations about Humboldt's private life and possible <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> continue to remain a fractious issue amongst scholars, particularly as earlier biographers had portrayed him as "a largely asexual, Christ-like Humboldt figure...suitable as a national idol."<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERupke2008195-7_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERupke2008195-7-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Illness_and_death">Illness and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Illness and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 February 1857, Humboldt suffered a minor <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a>, which passed without perceptible symptoms.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911-195">[195]</a></sup> It was not until the winter of 1858–1859 that his strength began to decline; on 6 May 1859, he died peacefully in Berlin, aged 89. His last words were reported to be "How glorious these sunbeams are! They seem to call Earth to the Heavens!"<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> His remains were conveyed in state through the streets of Berlin, in a hearse drawn by six horses. Royal chamberlains led the cortege, each charged with carrying a pillow with Humboldt's medals and other decorations of honor. Humboldt's extended family, descendants of his brother Wilhelm, walked in the procession. Humboldt's coffin was received by the prince-regent at the door of the cathedral. He was interred at the family resting-place at <a href="/wiki/Tegel" title="Tegel">Tegel</a>, along side his brother Wilhelm and sister-in-law Caroline.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955368-69_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDe_Terra1955368-69-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Publications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg/330px-Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg.png" width="330" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg/495px-Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg/660px-Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="973" data-file-height="389" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muisca_cyphers_acc_acosta_humboldt_zerda.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Muisca_numerals" title="Muisca numerals">Muisca numerals</a> as noted by <b>Humboldt</b></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Alexander von Humboldt published prolifically throughout his life. Many works were published originally in French or German, then translated to other languages, sometimes with competing translation editions. Humboldt himself did not keep track of all the various editions.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWulf2015413_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWulf2015413-198">[198]</a></sup> He wrote specialized works on particular topics of botany, zoology, astronomy, mineralogy, among others, but he also wrote general works that attracted a wide readership, especially his <i>Personal Narrative of Travels to the Equinoctial Regions of the New Continent during the years 1799-1804</i><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> His <i>Political Essay on the Kingdom of New Spain</i> was widely read in Mexico itself, the United States, as well as in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the original works have been digitally scanned by the Biodiversity Library.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> There have been new editions of print works, including his <i>Views of the Cordilleras and Monuments of the Indigenous Peoples of the Americas</i> (2014), which includes reproductions of all the color and black and white plates. In the original edition, the publication was in a large format and quite expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> There is a 2009 translation of his <i>Geography of Plants</i><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> and a 2014 English edition of <i>Views of Nature</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_works">Scientific works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Scientific works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
<ul>
<li><i>Florae Fribergensis specimen plantas cryptogramicus praesertim subterraneas exhibens</i>, 1793. Humboldt's observations of underground plants made when he was a mining inspector.</li>
<li><i>Versuche über die gereizte Muskel- und Nervenfaser nebst Versuchen über den chemischen Prozess des Lebens in der Thier- und Pflanzenwelt</i>. (2 volumes), 1797. Humboldt's experiments in galvanism and nerve conductivity.</li>
<li><i>Ueber die unterirdischen Gasarten und die Mittel ihren Nachteil zu verhindern</i>. Braunschwieg 1799.</li>
<li><i>Sur l'analyse de l'air atmosphérique</i>, with J.L. Gay-Lussac. Paris 1805. German edition, Türbingen.</li>
<li><i>Fragments de géologie et de climatologie asiatiques</i> 2 vols. Paris, 1831; Tübingen, 1831</li>
<li><i>Asie centrale, recherches sur les chaînes des montagnes et la climotologie comparée</i>. 3 vols. 1843</li>
</ul>
<p><i>Le voyage aux régions equinoxiales du Nouveau Continent, fait en 1799–1804, par Alexandre de Humboldt et Aimé Bonpland</i> (Paris, 1807, etc.), consisted of thirty folio and quarto volumes, including:</p>

Chicago: University of Chicago Press, 2014. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780226865065" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-226-86506-5</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/examencritiqued06humbgoog">Examen critique de l'histoire de la géographie du Nouveau Continent</a></i> (4 vols. 1814–1834)</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works">Other works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/79321"><i>Letters of Alexander von Humboldt to Varnhagen von Ense. From 1827 to 1858. With extracts from Varnhagen's diaries, and letters of Varnhagen and others to Humboldt. Tr. from the 2d German by Friedrich Kapp (ed.)</i></a>, biodiversitylibrary.org</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/item/78470"><i>Letters of Alexander von Humboldt written between the years 1827 and 1858 to Varnhagen von Ense together with extracts from Varnhagen's diaries, and letters of Varnhagen and others to Humboldt/ authorized translation from the German</i> (with explanatory notes and a full index of names)</a>, biodiversitylibrary.org</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.biodiversitylibrary.org/bibliography/640"><i>Nova genera et species plantarum</i> (7 vols. folio, 1815–1825), contains descriptions of above 4500 species of plants collected by Humboldt and Bonpland</a>, was mainly compiled by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Sigismund_Kunth" title="Carl Sigismund Kunth">Carl Sigismund Kunth</a>; J. Oltmanns assisted in preparing the <i>Recueil d'observations astronomiques</i> (1808); Cuvier, Latreille, Valenciennes and Gay-Lussac cooperated in the <i>Recueil d'observations de zoologie et d'anatomie comparée</i> (1805–1833).<sup id="cite_ref-EB1911_14-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EB1911-14">[14]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="notice metadata" style="text-align:left; border:0 solid #ddd; border-width:2px 0; padding: 0.5em 0;">The standard <a href="/wiki/List_of_botanists_by_author_abbreviation" class="mw-redirect" title="List of botanists by author abbreviation">author abbreviation</a> <b><span class="vcard"><span class="fn n"><span class="nickname">Humb.</span></span></span></b> is used to indicate this individual as the author when <a href="/wiki/Author_citation_(botany)" title="Author citation (botany)">citing</a> a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_name" title="Botanical name">botanical name</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours_and_namesakes">Honours and namesakes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Honours and namesakes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The honours which had been showered on Humboldt during life continued after his death. The first centenary of Humboldt's birth was celebrated on 14 September 1869, with great enthusiasm in both the New and Old Worlds. Numerous monuments were constructed in his honour, such as <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Park_(Chicago_park)" title="Humboldt Park (Chicago park)">Humboldt Park in Chicago</a>, planned that year and constructed shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Great_Chicago_Fire" title="Great Chicago Fire">Chicago fire</a>. Newly explored regions and species named after Humboldt, as discussed below, also stand as a measure of his wide fame and popularity.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1850: Knight Grand Cross in the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saints_Maurice_and_Lazarus" title="Order of Saints Maurice and Lazarus">Order of Saints Maurice and Lazarus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Species_named_after_Humboldt">Species named after Humboldt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Species named after Humboldt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(February 2015)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Humboldt described many geographical features and species that were hitherto unknown to Europeans. Species named after him include:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>Spheniscus humboldti</i> — <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_penguin" title="Humboldt penguin">Humboldt penguin</a></li>
<li><i>Dosidicus gigas</i> — <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_squid" title="Humboldt squid">Humboldt squid</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Lilium_humboldtii" title="Lilium humboldtii">Lilium humboldtii</a></i> — Humboldt's lily</li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Phragmipedium_humboldtii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Phragmipedium humboldtii (page does not exist)">Phragmipedium humboldtii</a></i> — an orchid</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_humboldtii" title="Quercus humboldtii">Quercus humboldtii</a></i> — South American (Andean) oak</li>
<li><i>Conepatus humboldtii</i> — <a href="/wiki/Humboldt%27s_hog-nosed_skunk" title="Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk">Humboldt's hog-nosed skunk</a></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Annona_reticulata" title="Annona reticulata">Annona humboldtii</a></i> — Neotropical fruit tree or shrub</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Utricularia_humboldtii" title="Utricularia humboldtii">Utricularia humboldtii</a></i> — a bladderwort</li>
<li><i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Geranium_humboldtii&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Geranium humboldtii (page does not exist)">Geranium humboldtii</a></i> — a cranesbill</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Salix_humboldtiana" title="Salix humboldtiana">Salix humboldtiana</a></i> — a South-American willow.<sup id="cite_ref-NRCS_salix_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRCS_salix-208">[208]</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Boto" title="Boto">Inia geoffrensis humboldtiana</a></i> — <a href="/wiki/Amazon_river_dolphin" title="Amazon river dolphin">Amazon river dolphin</a> subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Orinoco_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Orinoco River">Orinoco River</a> basin</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_features_named_after_Humboldt">Geographical features named after Humboldt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Geographical features named after Humboldt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Features named after him include:<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Bay_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Humboldt Bay (United States)">Humboldt Bay</a> — Bay in Northern California, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Current" title="Humboldt Current">Humboldt Current</a> - off the west coast of South America</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Glacier" title="Humboldt Glacier">Humboldt Glacier</a> - in North West Greenland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_River" title="Humboldt River">Humboldt River</a> - River in Nevada, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Peak_(Colorado)" title="Humboldt Peak (Colorado)">Humboldt Peak (Colorado)</a>&#160;– 4,287 m mountain in Custer County, Colorado, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pico_Humboldt" title="Pico Humboldt">Pico Humboldt</a>&#160;– 4,940 m mountain in Mérida, Venezuela</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Sink" title="Humboldt Sink">Humboldt Sink</a> - Dry lake bed in Nevada, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/East_Humboldt_Range" title="East Humboldt Range">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Humboldt_Range" title="West Humboldt Range">West Humboldt Range</a> in Nevada, United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sima_Humboldt" title="Sima Humboldt">Sima Humboldt</a> - sinkhole in Venezuela</li>
<li>"Monumento Nacional Alejandro de Humboldt" at <a href="/wiki/Caripe" title="Caripe">Caripe</a>, Venezuela</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mount_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mount Humboldt (page does not exist)">Mount Humboldt</a>&#160;– 1,617 m (5,308&#160;ft), New Caledonia</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Mountains_(Antarctica)" title="Humboldt Mountains (Antarctica)">Humboldt Mountains</a>, Antarctic mountains discovered and mapped by the <a href="/wiki/Third_German_Antarctic_Expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Third German Antarctic Expedition">Third German Antarctic Expedition</a> (1938–1939)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Range" title="Humboldt Range">Humboldt Range</a> - Mountain Range in Fiordland National Park, New Zealand</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Falls" title="Humboldt Falls">Humboldt Falls</a>&#160;– 275 m Water fall in Lower Hollyford Valley, Fiordland National Park, New Zealand</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Redwoods_State_Park" title="Humboldt Redwoods State Park">Humboldt Redwoods State Park</a> - in northern California, United States</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Places_named_after_Humboldt">Places named after Humboldt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Places named after Humboldt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities.2C_colleges.2C_and_schools">Universities, colleges, and schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Universities, colleges, and schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_University_of_Berlin" title="Humboldt University of Berlin">Humboldt University of Berlin</a> is named after Alexander and his brother <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm</a> who founded it<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Biological_Resources_Research_Institute" title="Alexander von Humboldt Biological Resources Research Institute">Alexander von Humboldt Biological Resources Research Institute</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogotá">Bogotá</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villa_de_Leiva" class="mw-redirect" title="Villa de Leiva">Villa de Leiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Humboldt_State_University" title="Humboldt State University">Humboldt State University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arcata,_California" title="Arcata, California">Arcata, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alejandro_de_Humboldt_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Alejandro de Humboldt University">Universidad Alejandro de Humboldt</a>, in Caracas, Venezuela</li>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alexander-von-Humboldt-Schule_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Alexander-von-Humboldt-Schule (disambiguation)">Alexander-von-Humboldt-Schule (disambiguation)</a></div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium,_Konstanz" title="Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium, Konstanz">Alexander-von-Humboldt-Gymnasium, Konstanz</a>, Germany</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Schule_Montr%C3%A9al" class="mw-redirect" title="Alexander von Humboldt Schule Montréal">German International School</a>, Montreal, Canada</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colegio_Alem%C3%A1n_Alexander_von_Humboldt_(Mexico_City)" title="Colegio Alemán Alexander von Humboldt (Mexico City)">Colegio Alemán Alexander von Humboldt</a>, Mexico City, Mexico</li>
<li>Colegio Peruano Alemán Alexander von Humboldt, Lima, Peru</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colegio_Humboldt,_Caracas" title="Colegio Humboldt, Caracas">Colegio Humboldt</a>, Caracas, Venezuela</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lecture_series">Lecture series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Lecture series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alexander von Humboldt also lends his name to a prominent lecture series in <a href="/wiki/Human_geography" title="Human geography">Human geography</a> in the Netherlands (hosted by the <a href="/wiki/Radboud_University_Nijmegen" title="Radboud University Nijmegen">Radboud University Nijmegen</a>). It is the Dutch equivalent of the widely known annual <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hettner" title="Alfred Hettner">Hettner</a> lectures at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Heidelberg" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Heidelberg">University of Heidelberg</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Alexander_von_Humboldt_Foundation">The Alexander von Humboldt Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: The Alexander von Humboldt Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After his death, Humboldt's friends and colleagues created the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Foundation" title="Alexander von Humboldt Foundation">Alexander von Humboldt Foundation</a> (<i>Stiftung</i> in German) to continue his generous support of young academics. Although the original endowment was lost in the <a href="/wiki/German_hyperinflation_of_the_1920s" class="mw-redirect" title="German hyperinflation of the 1920s">German hyperinflation of the 1920s</a>, and again as a result of World War II, the Foundation has been re-endowed by the German government to award young academics and distinguished senior academics from abroad. It plays an important role in attracting foreign researchers to work in Germany and enabling German researchers to work abroad for a period.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dedications">Dedications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Dedications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Poe" title="Edgar Allan Poe">Edgar Allan Poe</a> dedicated his last major work, <i><a href="/wiki/Eureka:_A_Prose_Poem" title="Eureka: A Prose Poem">Eureka: A Prose Poem</a></i>, to Humboldt, "With Very Profound Respect". Humboldt's attempt to unify the sciences in his <i>Kosmos</i> was a big inspiration for Poe's project.</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="citation gutenberg"><i><a href="http://www.gutenberg.org/etext/32037" class="extiw" title="gutenberg:32037">Eureka: A Prose Poem by Edgar Allan Poe</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/Project_Gutenberg" title="Project Gutenberg">Project Gutenberg</a></span></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ship">Ship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Ship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>

<p><i><a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_(ship)" title="Alexander von Humboldt (ship)">Alexander von Humboldt</a></i> is also a German ship named after the scientist originally built in 1906 by the German shipyard AG Weser at <a href="/wiki/Bremen_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bremen (city)">Bremen</a> as <i><b>Reserve Sonderburg</b></i>. She was operated throughout the North and Baltic Seas until being retired in 1986. Subsequently she was converted into a three masted <a href="/wiki/Barque" title="Barque">barque</a> by the German shipyard Motorwerke Bremerhaven and was re-launched in 1988 as <i>Alexander von Humboldt</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognitions_by_contemporaries">Recognitions by contemporaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Recognitions by contemporaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(February 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Simón Bolívar">Simón Bolívar</a> wrote that "The real discoverer of South America was Humboldt, since his work was more useful for our people than the work of all conquerors."<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Charles Darwin</a> expressed his debt to Humboldt, and admiration for his work,<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> writing to <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Dalton_Hooker" title="Joseph Dalton Hooker">Joseph Dalton Hooker</a> that Humboldt was the "<i>greatest scientific traveller who ever lived</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Humboldt" title="Wilhelm von Humboldt">Wilhelm von Humboldt</a> wrote that "Alexander is destined to combine ideas and follow chains of thoughts which would otherwise have remained unknown for ages. His depth, his sharp mind and his incredible speed are a rare combination." <a href="/wiki/Johann_Wolfgang_Goethe" class="mw-redirect" title="Johann Wolfgang Goethe">Johann Wolfgang Goethe</a> observed that "Humboldt showers us with true treasures." <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schiller" title="Friedrich Schiller">Friedrich Schiller</a> wrote that "Alexander impresses many, particularly when compared to his brother - because he shows off more!" <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_la_Luz_y_Caballero" title="José de la Luz y Caballero">José de la Luz y Caballero</a> wrote that "Columbus gave Europe a New World; Humboldt made it known in its physical, material, intellectual, and moral aspects." <a href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9on_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoléon Bonaparte">Napoléon Bonaparte</a> remarked "You have been studying Botanics? Just like my wife!" <a href="/wiki/Claude_Louis_Berthollet" title="Claude Louis Berthollet">Claude Louis Berthollet</a> said "This man is as knowledgeable as a whole academy." <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> remarked "I consider him the most important scientist whom I have met." <a href="/wiki/Emil_Du_Bois-Reymond" class="mw-redirect" title="Emil Du Bois-Reymond">Emil Du Bois-Reymond</a> wrote that "Every scientist is a descendant of Humboldt. We are all his family." <a href="/wiki/Robert_G._Ingersoll" title="Robert G. Ingersoll">Robert G. Ingersoll</a> wrote that "He was to science what Shakespeare was to the drama."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hermann_von_Helmholtz" title="Hermann von Helmholtz">Hermann von Helmholtz</a> wrote that "During the first half of the present century we had an Alexander von Humboldt, who was able to scan the scientific knowledge of his time in its details, and to bring it within one vast generalization. At the present juncture, it is obviously very doubtful whether this task could be accomplished in a similar way, even by a mind with gifts so peculiarly suited for the purpose as Humboldt's was, and if all his time and work were devoted to the purpose."<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>

London: John Murray. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-84854-898-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-84854-898-5">978-1-84854-898-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAlexander+von+Humboldt&amp;rft.aufirst=Andrea&amp;rft.aulast=Wulf&amp;rft.btitle=The+invention+of+nature+%3A+the+adventures+of+Alexander+von+Humboldt%2C+the+lost+hero+of+science&amp;rft.date=2015&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-84854-898-5&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=John+Murray&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
</ul>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_works_cited">Other works cited</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Other works cited">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><cite id="CITEREFBleichmar2012" class="citation book">Bleichmar, Daniela (2012). <i>Visible empire&#160;: botanical expeditions and visual culture in the Hispanic Enlightenment</i>. Chicago London: The University of Chicago Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-226-05853-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-226-05853-5">978-0-226-05853-5</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAlexander+von+Humboldt&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniela&amp;rft.aulast=Bleichmar&amp;rft.btitle=Visible+empire+%3A+botanical+expeditions+and+visual+culture+in+the+Hispanic+Enlightenment&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-226-05853-5&amp;rft.place=Chicago+London&amp;rft.pub=The+University+of+Chicago+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literary_works">Literary works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Literary works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kehlmann" title="Daniel Kehlmann">Daniel Kehlmann</a>'s 2005 novel <i>Die Vermessung der Welt</i>, translated into English by Carol Brown Janeway as <i><a href="/wiki/Measuring_the_World" title="Measuring the World">Measuring the World</a></i> in 2006, explores Humboldt's life through a lens of historical fiction, contrasting his character and contributions to science to those of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Carl Friedrich Gauss</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portal">Portal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alexander_von_Humboldt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Portal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.avh.de/en/index.htm">The Alexander von Humboldt Foundation</a></li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.avhumboldt.net">The Alexander von Humboldt Digital Library</a> A virtual research environment on the works of Alexander von Humboldt. A project by the University of Applied Sciences Offenburg and University of Kansas</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.avhumboldt.de">avhumboldt.de - Humboldt Informationen online</a> avhumboldt.de contains a large collection of data, texts and visuals concerning Alexander von Humboldt in German, English, Spanish and French. A project by the Chair of Romance Literatures, University of Potsdam (Germany).</li>
<li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://socgeo.ruhosting.nl/content/currentprogramme.html">Web site of the Humboldt Lecture series in Nijmegen, the Netherlands</a></li>
</ul>
